Cameron\nStation, Alexandria,\nVA.\n\nA Communication\n\nPublications.\n\n51\n\nReport\n\nPerspective.\n\nNewbury\n\nAPPENDIX\n\nNASA/DoD\n\nAEROSPACE\n\nDIFFUSION\n\nThe production,\n\ntransfer,\n\nKNOWLEDGE\n\nRESEARCH\nFact\n\nand use of scientific\n\nA\n\nPROJECT\n\nSheet\nand technical\n\ninformation\n\n(STI) is an essential\n\npart of aerospace\nR&D. We define STI production,\ntransfer, and use as Aerospace\nKnowledge\nDiffusion.\nStudies tell us that timely access to STI can increase productivity\nand innovation and\nhelp aerospace\nengineers\nand scientists maintain and improve their professional\nskills.\nThese\nsame studies remind us that we know little about aerospace\nknowledge\ndiffusion\nor about how\naerospace\nengineers and scientists\norganized\na research\nproject to\nDepartment\nof Defense (DoD), the\nis being conducted\nby researchers\n\nfind and use STI. To learn more about this process, we have\nstudy knowledge\ndiffusion.\nSponsored\nby NASA and the\nNASA/DoD\nAerospace Knowledge\nDiffusion Research Project\nat the NASA Langley Research Center, the Indiana University\n\nCenter for Survey Research, and Rensselaer\nPolytechnic\nInstitute.\nThis research is endorsed by\nseveral aerospace\nprofessional\nsocieties including the AIAA, RAeS, and DGLR and has been\nsanctioned\nby the AGARD and AIAA Technical\nInformation\nPanels.\nThis 4-phase project is providing descriptive\nand analytical data regarding\nthe flow of STI\nat the individual,\norganizational,\nnational, and international\nlevels.\nIt is examining\nboth the\nchannels used to communicate\nSTI and the social system of the aerospace\nknowledge\ndiffusion\nprocess.\nPhases 1 investigates\nthe information-seeking\nhabits and practices of U.S. aerospace\nengineers\nand scientists\nand places particular\nemphasis\non their use of government\nfunded\naerospace STI. Phase 2 examines the industry-government\ninterface and places special emphasis\non the role of the information\nintermediary\nin the knowledge\ndiffusion process.\nPhase 3 concerns\nthe academic-government\ninterface\nfaculty-student\ninterface.\nPhase\naerospace\nengineers\nand scientists\nSoviet Union.\nThe\nnational,\n\nand places specific emphasis on the information\nintermediary4 explores\nthe information-seeking\nbehavior\nof non-U.S.\nfrom Brazil, Western Europe, India, Israel, Japan, and the\n\nresults will help us to understand\nthe flow of STI at the individual,\norganizational,\nand international\nlevels.\nThe results of our research will contribute\nto increasing\n\nproductivity\nand to improving\nand\nengineers and scientists.\nThey can be\nand use, to plan new aerospace\nSTI\nmanagers,\ninformation\nmanagers, and\nof STI.
